Experts suggest that adults get between 7 and 9 [5] hours of slumber each night, which correlates to 5 or 6 full cycles. However, this amount can vary depending on your health and personal circumstances. For instance, if you are recovering from a cold, you will likely doze off longer than you would normally. Babies, children, and teens should get even more slumber. For example, a newborn baby needs between 14 and 17 hours of shuteye."

Each person is different, and therefore, you cannot count down a cycle to the exact minute. class="p4-blocks__block p4-blocks-byline"><div><span class="p4-blocks-byline__tooltip-container"><svg class="p4-blocks__icon" width="20" height="21" viewBox="0 0 20 21" fill="none" researchers, dietitians, and other professionals with expertise in sleep. They help ensure the content we publish is accurate, comprehensive, and based in the latest sleep science. See our <a href="https://sleepopolis.com/about/#experts" target="_blank" rel="noopener">full expert network</a>.</div></span><span class="p4-blocks-byline__expert">Expert Verified By: <a href="/experts/chaunie-brusie-rn/" target="_blank" title="Chaunie Brusie, RN, BSN">Chaunie Brusie, RN, BSN</a></span></div></div></div><p>It’s important to wake up after a completed sleep cycle —&nbsp;rather than mid-cycle — to feel refreshed and improve your sleep quality. Simply choose to set either your bedtime or wake up time and fill out the fields below, then hit the calculate button. The calculator uses this information to determine the best bedtime or wake time for you that includes an optimal number of complete sleep cycles.</p><section class="calculator__sleep-cycle"><div class="sleep-cycle__container sleep-cycle__container--quiz"><h2 class="sleep-cycle__heading">I want to calculate my…</h2><div class="sleep-cycle__quiz-tabs"><div class="sleep-cycle__quiz-tab active" data-tab="tab-wake">Wake Up Time</div><div class="sleep-cycle__quiz-tab" data-tab="tab-bed-time">Bed Time</div></div><div class="sleep-cycle__quiz--wake-up sleep-cycle__quiz-inner active" id="tab-wake"><p class="sleep-cycle__quiz-description">Calculate your wake up time by adding your age and when you plan on falling asleep.</p><form class="sleep-cycle__quiz-form" onsubmit="return!1" id="sleep-cycle--wake"><div class="sleep-cycle__quiz-question"><label class="sleep-cycle__input-label">What’s Your Age?<div class="sleep-cycle__tooltip-container"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="20" height="20" viewBox="0 0 20 20" fill="none"><path d="M10.8335 9.16665V14.1666H9.16683V9.16665H10.8335Z" fill="white"></path><path d="M10.8335 7.49998V5.83331H9.16683V7.49998H10.8335Z" fill="white"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M2.7085 9.99998C2.7085 5.9729 5.97309 2.70831 10.0002 2.70831C14.0272 2.70831 17.2918 5.9729 17.2918 9.99998C17.2918 14.0271 14.0272 17.2916 10.0002 17.2916C5.97309 17.2916 2.7085 14.0271 2.7085 9.99998ZM10.0002 3.95831C6.66344 3.95831 3.9585 6.66326 3.9585 9.99998C3.9585 13.3367 6.66344 16.0416 10.0002 16.0416C13.3369 16.0416 16.0418 13.3367 16.0418 9.99998C16.0418 6.66326 13.3369 3.95831 10.0002 3.95831Z" fill="white"></path></svg><div class="sleep-cycle__tooltip-wrapper tooltip-default"><div class="sleep-cycle__tooltip-content">Our sleep needs change all throughout our lives. p4-blocks-standard-byline__date--desktop"><span class="p4-blocks-standard-byline__update-icon"><svg class="p4-blocks__icon" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g clip-path="url(#clip0_5605_562)"><path d="M4.56005 7.20002C4.88005 5.60002 6.32005 4.40002 8.00005 4.40002C9.20005 4.40002 10.16 4.96002 10.8 5.84002L12.16 2025</div></div></section><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-7 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Formerly known as the Sleepytime Calculator, this tool helps get bedtime and wake up times just right.</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Have you ever noticed how some days you jump out of bed full of energy while on others, it’s a battle just to get moving? The culprit could be your sleep patterns, which affect many aspects of your mood, health, cognitive abilities, and energy levels. If you’re not getting optimal sleep for your age and lifestyle demands, you’re likely to feel far from your best self.</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">That’s why we’ve created a sleep calculator based on recommendations from health authorities such as the </span><a href="https://www.cdc.gov/sleep/about_sleep/how_much_sleep.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and the </span><a href="https://www.nhlbi.nih.gov/health/sleep/how-much-sleep" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">National Institutes of Health</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Our sleep calculator will give you insight into your ideal sleep schedule based on the number of sleep cycles you’re likely to attain. It’s also helpful to get a clearer picture of how many sleep cycles you might be getting when you enter your typical sleep patterns.&nbsp;</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">To get personalized advice for optimizing your sleep cycles, all you need to do is input the time you want to wake up or when you plan to fall asleep. It will then suggest the best times to fall asleep and show you the number of sleep cycles you will complete.</span></p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-8 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h2 class="wp-block-heading">Sleep Calculator: What Time Should I Go To Bed?</h2><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Since most people have daily commitments, the key to a great night’s rest will start with going to bed early enough to accommodate a consistent wake-up time. Consistently </span><a href="/blog/research-bedtime-adult-duke/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">going to bed at the same time</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> — even </span><a href="https://academic.oup.com/occmed/advance-article-abstract/doi/10.1093/occmed/kqae028/7659590?redirectedFrom=fulltext" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">on weekends</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> — helps regulate your circadian rhythms, or your internal clock, and improves your body’s ability to wake up naturally.&nbsp;</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">There are </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK526132/#:~:text=Sleep%20occurs%20in%20five%20stages,leading%20to%20progressively%20deeper%20sleep." target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">five sleep stages</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> in a cycle — wake, </span><a href="/education/n1-sleep/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">NI</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, </span><a href="/education/n2-sleep/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">N2</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, </span><a href="/education/n3-slow-wave-sleep/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">N3</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, and </span><a href="/education/rapid-eye-movement-sleep/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">REM</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> — which typically lasts </span><b>90-110 minutes</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">. </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK526132/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Research suggests</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> that getting </span><b>four to six cycles is ideal</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">, and being sure to complete full cycles will provide you with the best sleep experience.&nbsp;</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Over time, not going to bed at a consistent time can also create an irregular </span><a href="/education/circadian-rhythm/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">circadian rhythm</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, which further disrupts your sleep patterns and can </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5694588/#:~:text=In%20turn%2C%20through%20synaptic%20and,regulation%20and%20cause%20mood%20disturbances." target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">cause health problems</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, including mood disorders. Use the sleep calculator to plan a bedtime based on when you need to start your day, and try to stick to it consistently.</span></p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-9 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h2 class="wp-block-heading">Wake Calculator: What Time Should I Wake Up?</h2><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">It’s less about what time you should wake up and more about what part of the sleep cycle you wake up during. While getting </span><a href="https://www.cdc.gov/sleep/about_sleep/how_much_sleep.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">7 to 9 hours of sleep</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> each night is ideal, it’s also best not to wake up mid-sleep cycle. Since there are four sleep cycle stages (which last an average of 90 minutes), aiming to wake up at the end of your final cycle completes will give you the best shot at feeling refreshed and energized.</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Waking up in the </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK526132/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">middle of a sleep cycle</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> can make you feel disoriented and groggy and impacts mental functioning for 30 minutes or more. If your alarm goes off mid-REM, which is the </span><a href="/education/importance-of-rem-sleep/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">deepest sleep stage</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, you’ll likely </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4651462/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">feel tired and moody</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.&nbsp;</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Stage 1, or N1, is the first phase of the non-REM sleep cycle — it’s a light sleep where you switch between being awake and asleep. This stage lasts about 10 minutes and is the most natural stage from which you wake up. For the smoothest morning wake up, you can use the wake calculator to help you target wake up times that should be during your light sleep phase.</span></p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-16 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-10 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h2 class="wp-block-heading has-m-header-font-size">How Can I Optimize My Sleep Cycle?</h2><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">In addition to practicing </span><a href="/education/sleep-hygiene/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">good sleep hygiene</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, “hacking” your </span><a href="/education/stages-sleep-cycles/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">sleep cycles</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> can be hugely helpful in making sure you get enough shuteye and wake up refreshed. </span><b>The best way to optimize your sleep cycle is to allot enough time for 4-6 90-minute cycles, and to try to plan your wakeup time to land during a lighter sleep stage to avoid higher levels of grogginess and fatigue upon awakening. </b><span style="font-weight: 400;">Read on for more information about </span><a href="https://my.clevelandclinic.org/health/body/12148-sleep-basics" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">your sleep cycle</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and learn why it’s critical to spend enough time in each different phase.</span></p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-11 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h3 class="wp-block-heading">N1 Stage</h3><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This is the “dozing off” phase, where </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3375033/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">your body transitions</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> from being awake to falling asleep. It’s light, easy to wake up from, and lasts one to seven minutes. Your body starts to relax, your brain waves slow down, and you might experience those quirky twitches known as hypnic jerks.</span></p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-12 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h3 class="wp-block-heading">N2 Stage</h3><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">You’re asleep but not too deep during this stage. Your heart rate decreases, your upper airways relax, and your body temperature drops. About half of the time you spend asleep tends to be in this stage. Although sleep is still light in this stage, you’ll have less awareness of your surroundings. It’s an essential stage for </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC6053241/#:~:text=The%20critical%20contribution%20of%20N2,strong%20memories%20(Fig%207F)." target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">memory consolidation</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-13 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h3 class="wp-block-heading">N3 Stage</h3><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This is the deep, restorative sleep zone, usually starting about forty minutes after falling asleep. Blood pressure and heart rate drop, breathing slows and evens out, and the activity of sleep spindles in the brain decreases. During this time, your brain and body go through </span><a href="https://www.uhhospitals.org/health-information/health-and-wellness-library/article/adult-diseases-and-conditions-v1/stages-of-sleep" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">critical processes</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> like regulating hormones, consolidating memories, repairing tissues, and boosting your immune system. This stage is especially critical to waking up refreshed, and it’s also much harder to wake from this phase than N1 and N2.&nbsp;</span></p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-15 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h3 class="wp-block-heading">REM Stage</h3><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-14 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><p><a href="/education/importance-of-rem-sleep/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">REM sleep</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> occurs at the end of each cycle and is the lightest stage besides N1. The amount of time you spend in this stage gradually lengthens with each consecutive cycle, with the final one lasting about an hour. However, if you don’t get enough REM sleep during the night, you may </span><a href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/32809548/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">spend more time</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> in this stage on subsequent nights to make up for it. Dreaming is more likely in this stage, and your brain is as active as when you’re awake.&nbsp;</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">This stage is crucial for </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC8193556/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">memory and mood regulation</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Not getting enough REM sleep can lower immunity, impair hormone production, alter metabolism, and increase the risk for neurological diseases, such as dementia.</span></p></div></div><section id="block_be7559ec02a9525fbd159537e3cd29cd" class="p4-blocks__block p4-blocks-image-and-text p4-blocks-image-and-text__wrapper--icon p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading--alignleft"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--horizontal"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper-desktop"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper--icon"><img class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--image" src="https://i.sleepopolis.com/295/489/109/8/sleep-cycle_stage-1.webp" alt="Stage 1" width="144" height="145"></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__content-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__content-wrapper--icon"><h2 class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading--icon">Stage 1</h2><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__description p4-blocks-image-and-text__description--icon"><p>The dozing off phase</p></div></div></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper-mobile"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--mobile-content-wrapper"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper--icon"><img class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--image" src="https://i.sleepopolis.com/295/489/109/8/sleep-cycle_stage-1.webp" alt="Stage 1" width="144" height="145"></div><h2 class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading--icon">Stage 1</h2></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__description p4-blocks-image-and-text__description--icon"><p>The dozing off phase</p></div></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper-desktop"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper--icon"><img class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--image" src="https://i.sleepopolis.com/272/779/204/9/sleep-cycle_stage-2.webp" alt="Stage 2" width="144" height="145"></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__content-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__content-wrapper--icon"><h2 class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading--icon">Stage 2</h2><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__description p4-blocks-image-and-text__description--icon"><p>Asleep but not too deep</p></div></div></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper-mobile"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--mobile-content-wrapper"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper--icon"><img class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--image" src="https://i.sleepopolis.com/272/779/204/9/sleep-cycle_stage-2.webp" alt="Stage 2" width="144" height="145"></div><h2 class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading--icon">Stage 2</h2></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__description p4-blocks-image-and-text__description--icon"><p>Asleep but not too deep</p></div></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper-desktop"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper--icon"><img class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--image" src="https://i.sleepopolis.com/469/124/418/sleep-cycle_stage-3.webp" alt="Stage 3" width="144" height="145"></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__content-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__content-wrapper--icon"><h2 class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading--icon">Stage 3</h2><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__description p4-blocks-image-and-text__description--icon"><p>Deep sleep</p></div></div></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper-mobile"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--mobile-content-wrapper"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper--icon"><img class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--image" src="https://i.sleepopolis.com/469/124/418/sleep-cycle_stage-3.webp" alt="Stage 3" width="144" height="145"></div><h2 class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading--icon">Stage 3</h2></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__description p4-blocks-image-and-text__description--icon"><p>Deep sleep</p></div></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper-desktop"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper--icon"><img class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--image" src="https://i.sleepopolis.com/280/199/544/7/sleep-cycle_rem.webp" alt="Rem Stage" width="144" height="145"></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__content-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__content-wrapper--icon"><h2 class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading--icon">Rem Stage</h2><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__description p4-blocks-image-and-text__description--icon"><p>Rapid eye movement – the dreaming state</p></div></div></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--single-wrapper-mobile"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--mobile-content-wrapper"><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper p4-blocks-image-and-text__image-wrapper--icon"><img class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__icon--image" src="https://i.sleepopolis.com/280/199/544/7/sleep-cycle_rem.webp" alt="Rem Stage" width="144" height="145"></div><h2 class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading p4-blocks-image-and-text__heading--icon">Rem Stage</h2></div><div class="p4-blocks-image-and-text__description p4-blocks-image-and-text__description--icon"><p>Rapid eye movement – the dreaming state</p></div></div></div></section></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-18 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-17 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h2 class="wp-block-heading has-m-header-font-size">When to Wake Up: How Much Sleep Do I Need?</h2><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">While the general recommendation is to aim for 7 to 9 hours of sleep, the amount you need will be unique to </span><a href="https://www.nature.com/articles/s41467-018-08259-7" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">your biology</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and lifestyle. Babies, children, and teens need more sleep than adults to facilitate growth and learning. People who are </span><a href="/education/athletes-and-sleep/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">physically active</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and people dealing with or recovering from </span><a href="https://www.frontiersin.org/articles/10.3389/frsle.2022.1011930/full" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">illness or injury</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> tend to need more sleep.&nbsp;</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The </span><a href="https://newsinhealth.nih.gov/2021/04/good-sleep-good-health" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">quality of your sleep</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> will also significantly affect how effective your time in bed is. One significant factor that impacts sleep quality </span><a href="/education/sleep-and-aging/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">is age</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, with sleep issues becoming </span><a href="https://medlineplus.gov/ency/article/004018.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">more prevalent</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, especially in the senior years. If you wake up refreshed and energized throughout the day without relying on caffeine or other stimulants, you are likely getting enough sleep. Check out the chart below for </span><a class="rank-math-link" href="https://www.cdc.gov/sleep/about_sleep/how_much_sleep.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">how many hours of sleep you need</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> through all life stages according to the CDC:&nbsp;</span></p></div><figure class="wp-block-table"><table><tbody><tr><td>Newborn</td><td>0–3 months</td><td>14–17 hours (National Sleep Foundation)</td></tr><tr><td>Infant</td><td>4–12 months</td><td>12–16 hours per 24 hours, including naps (American Academy of Sleep Medicine)</td></tr><tr><td>Toddler</td><td>1–2 years</td><td>11–14 hours per 24 hours, including naps</td></tr><tr><td>Preschool</td><td>3–5 years</td><td>10–13 hours per 24 hours, including naps</td></tr><tr><td>School Age</td><td>6–12 years</td><td>9–12 hours per 24 hours</td></tr><tr><td>Teen</td><td>13–18 years</td><td>8–10 hours per 24 hours</td></tr><tr><td>Adult</td><td>18–60 years</td><td>7 or more hours per night</td></tr><tr><td>Older Adult</td><td>61–64 years</td><td>7–9 hours</td></tr><tr><td>Senior</td><td>65 years and older</td><td>7–8 hours</td></tr></tbody></table></figure><p>* All recommendations are based on a 24 hour day</p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-19 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h2 class="wp-block-heading has-m-header-font-size">The Effects of Sleep Deprivation on Your Body</h2><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Sleep deprivation can </span><a href="https://www.nhlbi.nih.gov/health/sleep-deprivation" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">affect many aspects of daily life</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, including</span><a href="https://www.nature.com/articles/d41586-023-02307-z" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;"> work productivity</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, safety, and overall health and wellbeing. In general, sleep deprivation </span><a href="https://www.frontiersin.org/articles/10.3389/fnbeh.2022.945661/full" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">can lead to immediate issues</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> such as fatigue, irritability, </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK547676/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">trouble concentrating, slower reaction times, and impaired judgment</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, as it prevents the brain from resting properly. Short-term effects also include daytime sleepiness, reduced alertness, mood swings, and </span><a href="https://www.dovepress.com/short--and-long-term-health-consequences-of-sleep-disruption-peer-reviewed-fulltext-article-NSS" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">memory issues</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, which are partly due to the accumulation of beta-amyloid proteins in the brain, associated with memory decline and a higher risk of dementia.</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Over time, the consequences of not getting enough sleep are </span><a href="https://www.cdc.gov/sleep/about_sleep/chronic_disease.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">more severe</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and include higher chances of obesity, heart disease, stroke, diabetes, and cognitive problems like memory loss and difficulty thinking. Long-term sleep deprivation can also exacerbate </span><a href="https://www.cdc.gov/pcd/issues/2021/20_0573.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">mental health issues</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> such as </span><a href="https://www.apa.org/pubs/journals/releases/bul-bul0000410.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">anxiety and depression</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-20 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h2 class="wp-block-heading has-m-header-font-size">Why Calculating Our Sleep Is Important</h2><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Calculating your sleep can help you time your sleep cycles so you wake up feeling refreshed, and it can also help make sure you’re spending enough time in each sleep stage and reaping the full benefits of a good night’s sleep — and avoiding the downsides of chronic sleep deprivation.&nbsp;</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">While how long you sleep matters, the quality and completion of sleep cycles are more crucial. In fact, </span><i><span style="font-weight: 400;">when</span></i><span style="font-weight: 400;"> you go to bed and wake up may be just as important as how long you sleep.&nbsp;</span></p><p><a href="https://doi.org/10.1093/sleep/zsad253" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Research shows</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> that sleep regularity, which is how consistent your sleep and wake times are from day to day, is linked to a significantly lower risk of dying from any cause compared to a sleep pattern that swings wildly. Plus, it may help </span><a href="https://doi.org/10.1093/sleep/zsad253" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">lower the risk</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> of death from cancer and cardiometabolic diseases like heart disease and diabetes in those with more consistent sleep patterns.&nbsp;</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Understanding and managing your sleep cycles with a sleep calculator </span><a href="https://doi.org/10.1139/apnm-2020-0032" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">could be key</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> to improving your health. Adjusting your sleep patterns and planning consistent sleep and wake times can ensure you complete these cycles, boosting your energy, lowering the risk of diseases, and potentially lengthening your lifespan.</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Are you wondering if a sleep calculator can make a difference for you? The best way to know is to try it out.&nbsp;</span></p></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-21 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h3 class="wp-block-heading has-m-header-font-size">What Happens During Sleep</h3><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Far from passive, during sleep, </span><a href="/education/sleep-and-the-brain/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">your brain</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> and </span><a href="/education/sleep-affects-body/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">body undergo</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> several processes affecting bodily systems, including body temperature, heart rate, metabolism, appetite, and restorative processes impacting everything from muscle repair to immune functions.&nbsp;</span></p><ul class="wp-block-list"><li><a href="https://www.frontiersin.org/articles/10.3389/fnins.2021.664781/full" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Body temperature drops</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> to conserve energy during sleep, with core temperature falling by one to two degrees.</span></li><li><a href="https://www.health.harvard.edu/blog/how-does-sleep-affect-your-heart-rate-2021012921846" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Heart rate slows down</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> during non-REM sleep stages and increases during REM sleep, with variations linked to dreaming activity.</span></li><li><a href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0026049516302049" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Metabolic rate decreases</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, affecting hunger hormones leptin and ghrelin, which influence appetite and energy balance.</span></li><li><a href="https://www.hopkinsmedicine.org/health/conditions-and-diseases/sleepwake-cycles" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Neurotransmitters and hormones like adenosine and melatonin are released</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. These chemicals build up to induce sleepiness and then diminish during sleep to increase alertness when you wake up. The pituitary gland </span><a href="https://my.clevelandclinic.org/health/articles/23309-human-growth-hormone-hgh" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">releases growth hormone</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, which helps repair small muscle tears from exercise and movement. Prolactin is released, which helps reduce inflammation and promotes joint recovery.&nbsp;</span></li><li><span style="font-weight: 400;">Even during deep sleep, </span><a href="https://www.ninds.nih.gov/health-information/public-education/brain-basics/brain-basics-understanding-sleep" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">the brain remains active</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, cleaning itself, processing emotions, and consolidating memories. Rapid Eye Movement (REM) sleep particularly plays a crucial role in stabilizing experiences into memory.</span></li></ul></div><div class="wp-block-group is-layout-constrained wp-container-core-group-is-layout-22 wp-block-group-is-layout-constrained"><h2 class="wp-block-heading has-m-header-font-size">How to Improve Your Sleep Quality</h2><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">How effectively do you prepare for a good night’s sleep? Making lifestyle choices that improve the quality of your sleep is one of the best ways to practice self-care.&nbsp;</span></p><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Practicing good sleep hygiene can help you fall asleep faster and get a more restful sleep, which will help you stay alert throughout the day. Here are some straightforward </span><a href="/education/sleep-hygiene/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">sleep hygiene tips</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> to optimize your sleep cycles:</span></p><ul class="wp-block-list"><li><span style="font-weight: 400;">Try to go to bed and wake up at the same time every day to support your </span><a href="/education/circadian-rhythm/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">circadian rhythm</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. (Yes, even on weekends when you can!)</span></li><li><span style="font-weight: 400;">Create a </span><a href="/education/nightly-rituals-and-routines-most-popular-survey/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">pre-sleep ritual</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> like reading a book or taking a warm bath. Find what signals your body it’s time to wind down.</span></li><li><span style="font-weight: 400;">Create an ideal</span><a href="/education/your-complete-guide-to-turning-your-bedroom-into-a-stress-free-sleep-oasis/"><span style="font-weight: 400;"> sleep environment</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">. Keep your bedroom cool, dark, and quiet.&nbsp;</span></li><li><span style="font-weight: 400;">Avoid heavy meals, </span><a href="/education/caffeine-and-sleep/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">caffeine</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">, and </span><a href="/education/alcohol-and-sleep/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">alcohol</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> before bed, and quit nicotine, as they can mess with your sleep cycle. Also do your best to eat enough nutritious food during the day, as </span><a href="https://www.piedmont.org/living-real-change/12-signs-you-may-not-be-eating-enough#:~:text=Sleep%20disturbances%3A%20Caloric%20restriction%20can,a%20harder%20time%20fighting%20infections." target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">eating too little</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> can also impact your sleep.</span></li><li><span style="font-weight: 400;">Get plenty of movement during the day, as </span><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC6045928/" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">regular exercise may improve your sleep</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> quality. Just try not to do it right before bedtime, or you may be too energized to sleep.</span></li><li><a href="/education/nap/"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Nap</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;"> wisely — too long or too late in the day can </span><a href="https://www.mayoclinic.org/healthy-lifestyle/adult-health/in-depth/napping/art-20048319#:~:text=Short%20naps%20generally%20don't,might%20interfere%20with%20nighttime%20sleep." target="_blank" rel="noopener"><span style="font-weight: 400;">disrupt nighttime sleep</span></a><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span></li></ul></div></div><hr class="wp-block-separator has-text-color has-so-blue-40-color has-alpha-channel-opacity has-so-blue-40-background-color has-background" style="margin-top:48px;margin-bottom:48px"><section id="block_c08eb5bb98790ffde1fb8c3bb64af794" class="p4-blocks__block p4-blocks-accordion p4-blocks-accordion--default"><h2 class="p4-blocks-accordion__heading">FAQs</h2><details open=""><summary><svg class="p4-blocks__icon" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path d="M6 0h4v16H6z"></path><path d="M0 6h16v3.93H0z"></path></svg> <span>How many hours of sleep is recommended?</span></summary><div><p>Adults need 7 or more hours per night, according to the&nbsp;<a href="https://aasm.org/resources/pdf/pressroom/adult-sleep-duration-consensus.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener">American Academy of Sleep Medicine</a>. However, the hours of sleep a person needs vary by age, health, and lifestyle. For instance, if you are pregnant, sick, or recovering from an injury or surgery, you’ll need more sleep. Infants and&nbsp;<a href="http://v/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">children also need more sleep</a>&nbsp;than adults.</p></div></details><details><summary><svg class="p4-blocks__icon" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path d="M6 0h4v16H6z"></path><path d="M0 6h16v3.93H0z"></path></svg> <span>Is it normal to still feel tired after sleeping for 8 hours?</span></summary><div><p>Feeling tired&nbsp;<a href="/education/why-am-i-tired-after-8-hours-of-sleep/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">even after sleeping for 8 hours</a>&nbsp;can be confusing, but it is often due to factors such as previous sleep loss, poor sleep quality, or disturbances to your body’s natural sleep-wake cycle. If feeling tired after what feels like a good night’s sleep becomes a frequent occurrence, you may want to consult with your healthcare provider to rule out any underlying medical conditions.</p></div></details><details><summary><svg class="p4-blocks__icon" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path d="M6 0h4v16H6z"></path><path d="M0 6h16v3.93H0z"></path></svg> <span>What is sleep debt and how do I know if I have it?</span></summary><div><p>function at their best. For example, if you need eight hours of sleep and only get six, you’ve accumulated two hours of sleep debt in one night. If you’ve accumulated enough sleep debt, you might also feel groggy, irritable, or experience other&nbsp;<a href="/education/sleep-deprivation/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">symptoms of sleep deprivation</a>&nbsp;throughout the day.</p><p>You can use our&nbsp;<a href="/calculators/sleep-debt-calculator/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Sleep Debt Calculator</a>&nbsp;to figure out how much sleep debt you’ve accumulated and to get your sleep habits back on track.</p></div></details></section><div style="height:24px" aria-hidden="true" class="wp-block-spacer"></div><section id="block_f124462b291e0afaab080d2b4612cc6b" class="p4-blocks__block p4-blocks-biography"><div class="p4-blocks-biography__container"><div class="p4-blocks-biography__wrapper"><div class="p4-blocks-biography__image"><img src="https://i.sleepopolis.com/414/949/853/3/new-sleepopolis-about-us-page.webp" alt="Sleepopolis Team" width="2000" height="1132"></div><div class="p4-blocks-biography__designations"><h2 class="p4-blocks-biography__name">Sleepopolis Team</h2></div></div><div class="p4-blocks-biography__wrapper"><div class="p4-blocks-biography__about"><h3 class="p4-blocks-biography__heading">About Author</h3><div class="p4-blocks-biography__about"><p>The Sleepopolis team is all about helping you sleep better. We live, eat, breathe, and sleep (ha!) all things, well, sleep! Whether you need a new mattress, are having trouble sleeping, or are just tired of counting sheep, we’ve got you covered. Check back here often for the latest and greatest in mattress reviews, sleep news, or health tips, and in the meantime, sleep well.</p></div></div></div></div></section></div></div><footer
